People v. Diller


C030442


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 1165; 85 Cal. Rptr. 2d 720; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 570; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4589; 99 Daily Journal DAR 5858



June 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied September 15, 1999 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6360.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 98F00794. Jeffrey L. Gunther, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed decision from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), in an action regarding the sale of methamphetamine in which the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss prior strike allegation regarding his burglary charge sustained when he was seventeen.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold methamphetamine to an undercover agent on two occasions and was charged with selling the drug. Six years earlier, when defendant was seventeen, he was adjudged a ward of the court following a sustained petition alleging first-degree burglary. Plaintiff amended complaint to add the allegation of a prior strike regarding the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the prior charge. Defendant entered a plea of no contest to the drug charges. He was sentenced to prison and obtained a certificate of probable cause to bring the appeal. The appellate court reversed the order due to the statutory rules of construction, thus defendant's juvenile adjudication for the serious and violent felony of first-degree burglary, that would have been a strike if committed by an adult, was not counted as a conviction or a prior strike.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order denying defendant's motion to dismiss prior strike regarding juvenile burglary charge since his juvenile adjudication for serious and violent felony of first-degree burglary was not counted as a conviction to be used as a prior strike based on legislative intent.

 

351 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Gerawan Farming, Inc. v. Veneman


F031142


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 1025; 85 Cal. Rptr. 2d 598; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 556; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4464; 99 Daily Journal DAR 5679



June 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 1, 1999 (S080610), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6107.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of November 27, 2000 Reported at: 24 Cal. 4th 468.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Super. Ct. No. 94-167877. Howard R. Broadman and Patrick J. O'Hara, Judges. * 


* Judge Broadman granted the motion for judgment on the pleadings without leave to amend and rendered the final judgment from which the appeal is taken.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California) that granted judgment on the pleadings to respondent Secretary of the California Department of Food and Agriculture in appellant's action challenging the administrative order that established the Plum Marketing Board of California.


OVERVIEW: A California marketing order established the California Plum Marketing Board, a mandatory marketing program for plum producers. Appellant producer filed a complaint challenging the order. Respondent Secretary of the California Department of Food and Agriculture moved for judgment on the pleadings. The trial court granted respondent's motion. Appellant filed an amended complaint, asserting only California Constitution free speech and association causes of action. The trial court granted respondent's renewed motion for judgment on the pleadings. Appellant sought on appeal to distinguish the California marketing order from a similar federal order and argued that the California Constitution provided an independent basis to invalidate the order. The appellate court affirmed. The federal marketing order was essentially the same as the California marketing order, and there were no cogent reasons or independent state interests that supported a departure from the U.S. Supreme Court's analysis in upholding the validity of the federal marketing order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of judgment on the pleadings to respondent, ruling that the administrative order did not violate relevant provisions of the California Constitution.

 

352 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Hi-Voltage Wire Works, Inc. v. City of San Jose


H018407


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 600; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 885; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 527; 76 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P46,134; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4016; 99 Daily Journal DAR 5056



May 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 1, 1999 (S080318), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6105.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of November 30, 2000 Reported at: 24 Cal. 4th 537.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Super. Ct. No. CV768694. Richard C. Turrone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and others, appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which held that their municipal program violated Cal. Const. art. I, § 31 because it accorded an advantage to certain subcontractors based on their race or sex.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, a city and others, designed a municipal program to increase participation by minority and women businesses in public construction projects. Plaintiffs, a contracting firm and a taxpayer, brought suit, alleging the program was unconstitutional under Cal. Const. art. I, § 31. That provision prohibited governmental entities from discriminating against or granting preferential treatment in certain public operations. The trial court held that the program violated the state constitution because it accorded an advantage to certain subcontractors based on their race or sex. The trial court therefore enjoined defendants from implementing the program. The defendants appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's order because the means that the defendants employed to counteract subcontracting discrimination constituted preferential treatment of certain groups. Therefore, the court held that the groups were given an unconstitutional advantage over other businesses.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that held that defendants' municipal program violated the state constitution because it gave unconstitutional preferential treatment to certain groups due to race or sex.

 

353 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Fowler


No. F025927.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 581; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 874; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 529; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4014; 99 Daily Journal DAR 5053



May 26, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II, III, and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. 64990. Jerold L. Turner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We remand for the limited purpose of conducting a Romero hearing. (People v. Superior Court (Romero) (1996) 13 Cal. 4th 497 [53 Cal. Rptr. 2d 789, 917 P.2d 628].) In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California) because the trial court was not aware it had discretion to strike one or more of his prior serious felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in oral copulation while confined in a detention center. In addition, appellant had a prior juvenile adjudication for rape and an adult rape conviction within the definition of the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667. Appellant challenged his sentence enhancement, claiming it violated his U.S. Constitutional rights. Appellant alleged that the court improperly considered a juvenile adjudication in which he did not have a trial by jury and did not waive his right to a trial by a jury. The court held that the lower court properly considered the juvenile matter because appellant had demonstrated a propensity toward criminal activity and that his failure to learn from his previous mistakes warranted a harsher adult sentence. The case was remanded to determine whether a prior strike should be stricken in the interests of justice, however.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's application of the three strikes statute even though it considered a juvenile conviction. The court found that appellant had failed to draw any lessons from his prior judicial determinations and his conduct warranted a more severe punishment.

 

354 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Guardianship of Zachary H.


No. H017530.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


73 Cal. App. 4th 51; 86 Cal. Rptr. 2d 7; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 609; 99 Daily Journal DAR 6541



May 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 24, 1999. Review Denied September 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6585.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County. Super. Ct. No. PRO40455. William M. Kelsay, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order, comprised of the order after hearing and order appointing guardian, is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County (California) that granted a guardianship petition and appointed respondents as minor child's guardians.


OVERVIEW: Mother and appellant father were estranged lovers. Child was born of the union and mother immediately placed child with respondents, prospective adoptive parents. Appellant father successfully resisted petitions to terminate his parental rights and to adopt child. Appellant filed a motion for custody of child and, alternatively, for visitation. Mother opposed the motion and supported the existing custody. Respondents filed a guardianship petition. Mother filed a pleading seeking physical custody in the event custody was to be awarded to persons other than respondents. The trial court granted respondents' guardianship petition. On appeal, the court affirmed. Child had enjoyed stable placement with respondents since his birth, and the mandatory return feature of Cal. Fam. Code § 8804(c) could not supersede child's constitutional right to such placement. Appellant's other arguments to the contrary were unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the guardianship petition on the ground that child had acquired a constitutional right to placement with respondents.

 

355 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. Fresno Irrigation Dist.


No. F028993.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 147; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 775; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 478; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3641; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 130; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4619



May 17, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 9, 1999. Review Denied August 25, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6066.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Super. Ct. No. 554161-0. Franklin P. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Each party is to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant irrigation district appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) holding that plaintiff employee was not required to exhaust an internal grievance procedure prior to filing suit for wrongful termination, that plaintiff was not in a safety-sensitive position, and that a random drug test violated plaintiff's constitutional right to privacy and his right to be free of unreasonable searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed that part of a judgment holding that plaintiff employee's suit was not barred by his failure to exhaust defendant irrigation district's internal grievance procedure but reversed that part holding that a random drug test violated his constitutional right to privacy and his right to be free of unreasonable searches and seizures. Whether plaintiff held a safety-sensitive position, which would justify a random drug test, was a mixed question of law and fact involving values underlying legal principles, and therefore de novo review was appropriate. The court concluded that plaintiff's position was correctly designated safety-sensitive because there existed both a hazardous working environment and hazards inherent in the work itself. Plaintiff's privacy interests were diminished by the fact that defendant gave six months notice before implementing the drug-testing policy. Moreover, plaintiff's privacy interests were outweighed by defendant's legitimate and substantial safety-related reasons for randomly drug testing its construction and maintenance workers. Therefore, the random drug test did not violate plaintiff's constitutional's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding that plaintiff was not required to exhaust internal grievance procedures before filing a suit for wrongful termination and reversed the holding that plaintiff's constitutional rights were violated by a random drug test. Plaintiff's job was properly classified as safety-sensitive, and defendant's interests in minimizing the risk of harm to employees outweighed plaintiff's privacy interests.

 

356 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Plaza Hollister Ltd. Partnership v. County of San Benito


No. H016763.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


72 Cal. App. 4th 1; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 715; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 471; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3540; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4515



May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1999. Review Denied August 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5667.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Benito County. Super. Ct. No. 18179. Thomas P. Breen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the motion to vacate is reversed and the trial court is directed to vacate the stipulated judgment upon remand. Each party shall bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and intervenor, a county tax assessor, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Benito County (California) denying appellant's motion to vacate a stipulated judgment, which reduced the base-year value of respondent taxpayer's apartment complex property and provided for refunds from 1984 forward based on the value recalculation.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed an order denying the motion of appellant, a county tax assessor, to vacate a judgment in respondent taxpayer's tax refund action stipulated to by respondent, the county board of supervisors (CBS). The judgment, to which appellant was not a party, reduced the base-year value of respondent's apartment complex property and provided for refunds from 1984 forward based on the value recalculation. The court, finding that it had authority to reject an unjust stipulation and that appellant had standing to appeal a void judgment that revised base-year value and reduced assessments, concluded that the judgment was void because it granted relief that the lower court had no power to grant in the exercise of its subject matter jurisdiction. The exercise of judgment as to the value of the property was conferred only on the county board of equalization (CBE). Respondent CBS could not confer jurisdiction upon the lower court to equalize individual assessments, and remand was necessary to allow the CBE to determine value. Furthermore, the lower court had no authority to retroactively apply a reduction in base-year value to years predating the assessment appeal.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant assessor's motion to vacate the stipulated judgment on appellee's tax refund action was reversed and remanded. The court found that the exercise of judgment as to base-year value and assessment reductions was conferred solely on the board of equalization. Therefore, the lower court lacked subject matter jurisdiction and its judgment was void.

 

357 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Brunson v. Department of Motor Vehicles


No. B116873.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


72 Cal. App. 4th 1251; 85 Cal. Rptr. 2d 710; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 581; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4669; 99 Daily Journal DAR 5942



May 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 11, 1999. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 11, 1999 on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at: 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 580. Review Denied August 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5573.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS032384. Diane Wayne and David Yaffee, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the petition is dismissed. Each party to bear its own costs of appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted a petition for a writ of mandate prohibiting appellant Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV) from requiring respondents to provide their Social Security numbers in order to obtain new or renewed drivers' licenses and/or DMV identification cards as required under Cal. Veh. Code § 1635.5.


OVERVIEW: Respondents filed a petition for a writ of mandate against appellant Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV), seeking to enjoin appellant from refusing to accept respondents' applications for drivers' licenses and DMV identification cards due to respondents' failure to provide their Social Security numbers on the DMV application as required by Cal. Veh. Code § 1653.5. Respondents objected to providing their Social Security numbers on religious grounds. The trial court granted the petition, finding that the burden on respondents far outweighed any inconvenience to appellant. The appellate court reversed the judgment, holding that the trial court erred in applying the compelling state interest test to respondents' free exercise of religion challenge. The court found that the statutory requirement that applicants provide a Social Security number met the rational basis test because it was wholly neutral in religious terms and uniformly applicable. Because § 1653.5 was a rational means of achieving a legitimate governmental end, the court held that it survived scrutiny under the rational basis standard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment and dismissed respondents' petition for a writ of mandate to prohibit appellant Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV) from requiring respondents to provide their Social Security numbers on DMV applications where the trial court erred in applying the compelling state interest test to respondents' free exercise of religion challenge because the statute was wholly neutral in religious terms and uniformly applicable.

 

358 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Martinez


No. H018197.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 1502; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 638; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 468; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3506; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4449



May 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied August 25, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 6078.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Super. Ct. No. 192941. Leonard B. Sprinkles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which, due to defendant's three prior "strike" felonies, sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant contended that his sentence was unconstitutionally cruel or unusual.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had three prior serious felony convictions, was charged and convicted with the felonies of possessing methamphetamine and attempting by threat to deter a peace officer from carrying out his duty, and the misdemeanors of driving under the influence, driving with a blood-alcohol level over the legal limit, and using phencyclidine. Due to defendant's three prior "strike" felonies, he was sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant contended on appeal that his sentence was unconstitutionally cruel or unusual. The court held that after considering the nature of the offender, defendant's recidivism warranted lengthy incarceration. Defendant was a repeat offender who seemingly had not learned from past incarceration. Defendant's prior felonies involved express and implicit threats of violence. The record indicated that defendant had been prone to violence or the threat of violence. Further, simply because California's repeat offender, or "three strikes" statute, was among the most extreme did not compel the conclusion that it was unconstitutionally cruel or unusual. The court concluded that defendant's sentence did not shock its conscience.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court below, which sentenced defendant to life imprisonment, on the grounds that given defendant's prior history, the sentence did not shock the court's conscience.

 

359 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



City of Burbank v. Burbank-Glendale-Pasadena Airport Authority


No. B123632.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


72 Cal. App. 4th 366; 85 Cal. Rptr. 2d 28; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 506; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4822



May 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published May 20, 1999.
Rehearing Denied June 1, 1999. Review Denied August 11, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5393.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles. Super. Ct. No. EC022341. Carl J. West, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Appellants shall recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city and intervenor state appealed a decision from the Superior Court of the County of Los Angeles granting defendant authority summary judgment based on its finding that city had delegated its powers under Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 21661.6 to authority and was without power to enforce the statute as against it.


OVERVIEW: Defendant authority was created to acquire and run the local airport. Authority was granted all statutory powers and the rights of eminent domain. Using said rights, authority acquired property to update the facility. Plaintiff held a public meeting, pursuant to Cal. Pub. Util. § 21661.6, and withheld approval. Plaintiff city sought injunctive and declaratory relief to enjoin authority from using the land without approval and to affirm the validity of § 21661.6. The trial court ruled in favor of defendant, based on its finding that city had delegated its powers to authority and could not challenge it. City and state intervenor appealed. The court held that all agencies, as well as city, were subject to the approval process under Cal. Gov. Code § 53091. This did not create a veto power. The city could not delegate its discretionary powers in a way as to totally abdicate them. The court found that control of airplanes had been preempted by the federal government, but not the land. City could use its police powers to help mitigate noise. Section 21661.6 was not unconstitutional just because some entity could misuse it.


OUTCOME: The court found that Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 21661.6 was valid and constitutional and reversed the decision denying plaintiff city's right's under the code to restrict defendant's building plans to mitigate noise.

 

360 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Filet Menu, Inc. v. Cheng


No. B118633.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


71 Cal. App. 4th 1276; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 384; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 447; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3268; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4216



May 4, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC168920. Peter D. Lichtman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Appellant is awarded its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that sustained defendant customer's demurrer to an action alleging, inter alia, breach of a contract for the purchase of restaurant supplies for defendant's business in Canada, after ruling that the tolling provisions of the statute of limitations, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 351, violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Several years after defendant customer failed to pay for restaurant supplies that were ordered and delivered to his business in Canada, plaintiff company sued for, inter alia, breach of contract. California was defendant's place of residence and plaintiff's place of business. Defendant demurred, pursuant to the statute of limitations, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 351. The demurrer was sustained, with the trial court ruling that the tolling provisions of § 351 for a defendant's absence from the state impermissibly burdened persons engaged in interstate commerce and violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. Plaintiff appealed. In reversing, the court agreed that § 351 imposed an unconstitutional burden on residents who traveled in the course of interstate commerce that was not shared by residents involved in local trade. However, the tolling provisions did not violate the Commerce Clause with respect periods of out-of-state travel that were unrelated to interstate commerce. Since plaintiff's complaint did not specify the extent to which defendant's absences were in the course of interstate commerce, application of § 351 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining the demurrer was reversed because defendant was absent from his residence in the state for periods sufficient to toll the running of the statute of limitations and because plaintiff's complaint did not describe the extent to which those absences were in the course of interstate commerce, so they did not establish that application of the tolling provisions violated the Commerce Clause.

Malone v. Superior Court


F031234, F031970


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 1289; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 533; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 451; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3322; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4240



May 4, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 21, 1999 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4963.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING; petition for writ of mandate and/or prohibition. Super. Ct. No. 73461.



DISPOSITION: The petitions for writ of mandate and/or prohibition are denied and the order to show cause discharged. Stay of trial previously ordered is vacated upon finality of this court's decision herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The cause was to be heard on a petition for writ of mandate and/or prohibition brought by petitioners, people who had been charged with committing various offenses, including murder, carjacking robbery, and kidnapping, and had pled not guilty.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were charged with committing various offenses, including attempted premeditated murder, carjacking, robbery, and kidnapping during the commission of a car jacking. They demurred, claiming lack of jurisdiction, but the demurrers were overruled. They pled not guilty. Petitioners then filed motions to dismiss, which were denied. They then filed a petition for writ of mandate and/or prohibition and request for stay, which was denied. A petition for review was granted. The matter was transferred with direction to vacate the order denying mandate and to issue an alternative writ. Petitioners filed a petition for writ of mandate and/ or prohibition and request for stay, or, alternatively, to join two case numbers. The court ordered two cases consolidated and issued an order to show cause and stayed the trial date. The court allowed the parties an opportunity to file additional briefing and then denied the petitions for writ of mandate and/or prohibition and discharged the order to show cause. The stay of the trial was also vacated. The court rejected petitioners' jurisdictional and vicinage challenges.


OUTCOME: The court found jurisdiction was proper and denied the petitions for writ of mandate and/or prohibition and discharged the order to show cause and the stay of the trial.

 

362 of 1449 DOCUMENTS




Norwest Mortgage, Inc. v. Superior Court


No. D032050.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


72 Cal. App. 4th 214; 85 Cal. Rptr. 2d 18; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 487; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3706; 99 Daily Journal DAR 4696



April 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Mandate from an Order of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. N73741. David B. Moon, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of mandate issue directing the superior court to vacate its September 14, 1998, order granting plaintiffs' motion to certify the class action, and to enter a new and different order denying plaintiffs' motion for certification of a nationwide class, without prejudice to any motion for certification of a different class or classes consistent with our opinion. The temporary stay is vacated. Petitioner is entitled to costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgage company sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that granted nationwide class certification in an action brought by plaintiffs that alleged defendant's forced placement insurance program was an unfair business practice under California's unfair competition law pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought action against defendant mortgage company that alleged its forced placement insurance (FPI) program was an unfair business practice under California's unfair competition law (UCL) pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 et seq. Plaintiffs were granted nationwide class certification, and defendant appealed. In reversing the order, the court identified three categories of class members and held Category III members, non-California residents for whom defendant's conduct of purchasing FPI in states other than California, could not assert the UCL claim. Plaintiffs did not cite any authority that construed the UCL as applicable to claims of non-California residents injured by conduct occurring beyond California's borders. The 1992 amendment clarified the scope of injunctive relief available to a plaintiff who was already entitled to pursue a claim under the UCL, but did not expand the conduct regulated by the UCL. Diamond did not support plaintiffs' effort to include Category III members in the nationwide class. The choice of law rules never became relevant because there was no issue to be evaluated with respect to the claims of Category III members.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted plaintiffs' motion to certify the class action, holding the unfair competition law claim could not form the basis for the nationwide class because the claims of non-California residents for whom defendant's conduct of purchasing forced placement insurance occurred in states other than California (Category III members) would be arbitrary and unfair and transgress due process limitations.


 

363 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



City v. Freeman


No. A082244.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


71 Cal. App. 4th 869; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 132; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 360; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3037; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3893



April 27, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Super. Ct. No. 13212. Marjorie A. Slabach, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: The child support order is reversed and remanded to the trial court for recomputation in accordance with the mandate of section 4071.5. In the interests of justice each party shall bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the city and county of San Francisco, challenged a child support order from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), that was calculated including two hardship deductions, in noncompliance with Cal. Fam. Code § 4071.5, for respondent father's two resident children. The trial court held § 4071.5 should not have applied because it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the city and county of San Francisco, sought review of a child support order calculated by granting to respondent father, in contravention of the provisions of Cal. Fam. Code § 4071.5, two hardship deductions for his resident children. The order was premised on a holding that § 4071.5 was unconstitutional. The court held § 4071.5 was not subject to strict scrutiny because the statutory classification between children whose parents could and could not claim the hardship deduction was not based on an immutable trait or a disfavored characteristic. Even if the right of the resident children to be supported by respondent was fundamental, the burden on that right was indirect and uncertain where the amount of money used to support the resident children was subject to other laws, economic factors, and parental choices. The court also held § 4071.5 was not violative of equal protection because it was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of maximizing recoupment from parents of public funds spent for their children's basic needs. Accordingly, the child support order was reversed and remanded for recomputation in accordance with § 4071.5.


OUTCOME: The child support order was reversed, and was remanded for recomputation of support, because respondent father was not entitled to two hardship deductions for his resident children. The challenged statutory provision was not unconstitutional because it was not subject to strict scrutiny, and it was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of maximizing recoupment from parents of public funds spent for their children's basic needs.

 

364 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Torres


C028359


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 704; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 96; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 353; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2968; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3831



April 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted August 11, 1999 (S079575), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5320.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2001 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of May 21, 2001, Reported at: 25 Cal. 4th 680.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Yolo County. Super. Ct. No. 10978. James L. Stevens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of Yolo County (California) that committed him to two years in a state mental hospital under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his commitment to two years in a state mental hospital as a sexually violent predator and contended the trial court erred by overruling his objection to the use of noncertified documents to prove his out-of-state prior convictions. The court stated that nothing in the Sexually Violent Predators Act (the act), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq., suggested any legislative intent to create an exception to the mandate of Cal. Evid. Code §§ 1530 and 1531 that a writing be certified before it was introduced into evidence. The court held that because a person's liberty interest was at stake in a proceeding under the act, he or she had the right of confrontation and cross-examination, and without the safeguard of certification, the hearsay in writings was not sufficiently trustworthy to be admitted and used against defendant. After rejecting defendant's other assertions of error, the court held defendant's out-of-state prior convictions were improperly proved by noncertified documents, reversed the order of commitment, and remanded the case for a limited retrial of the question whether sufficient evidence supported the requisite prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of commitment and remanded the matter for the limited purpose of a retrial of the question whether the finding of the requisite prior convictions was supported by sufficient evidence.

 

365 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Sutter's Place v. Kennedy


No. H017471.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 674; 84 Cal. Rptr. 2d 84; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 351; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2944; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3803



April 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County. No. CV764875. John A. Flaherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The parties shall bear their own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff card room operator appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted a summary judgment in favor of defendant district attorney and issued a permanent injunction barring plaintiff from continuing fee collection practices.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attorney general notified plaintiff card room operator that his collection fees violated Cal. Penal Code § 330 because plaintiff charged each bettor a fee based on the number of bets placed and charged a higher fee for tables with higher betting limits. When plaintiff brought an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, the trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, issued a permanent injunction barring plaintiff from continuing his fee collection practices, and denied plaintiff's motion for a new trial. On appeal, plaintiff asserted its fee collection practices were permissible under the newly enacted Cal. Penal code § 337(j). The court agreed and held that the legislature's September 1998 revision of § 337(j) explicitly authorized plaintiff's fee collection practices, was not unconstitutional, and was properly enacted as urgency legislation. The court stated defendant's concerns had been specifically addressed by the legislature's adoption of a comprehensive fee collection scheme and reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment because legislation passed subsequent to the decision authorized plaintiff's fee collection practices.

People v. Willis


F026866


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 530; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 895; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 337; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3671; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2850



April 20, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] CERTIFIED FOR PARTIAL PUBLICATION - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II., III., and IV. of Discussion identified as [NOT CERTIFIED FOR PUBLICATION].

NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted August 11, 1999 (S079245), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5317.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2001 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2002 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2003 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. 66919. Clarence Westra, Jr. and Kenneth C. Twisselman II, Judges. * 


*  Judge Westra ruled on the suppression motion; Judge Twisselman presided at trial.

.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of Superior Court of Kern County (California), which held that police officers' warrantless entry and search of his hotel room did not violate the U.S. Const. amend. IV, and therefore evidence seized as a result of the search was properly admitted at his trial for possession of methamphetamine for sale and possession of narcotics paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: Police officers received information that there was excessive foot and phone traffic into and out of appellant's motel room, who was a convicted sex offender and transferred parolee on active parole. Officers went to the room, announced their presence, and stated they were there to do a parole search. Upon opening the door, officers saw a knife sheath and a syringe lying on a dresser. Appellant told officers that he was discharged from parole, and officer secured the area until they could verify the information. During this time, the officer interviewed a woman in the room, who admitted to taking drugs and stated that there was drugs paraphernalia in a nearby briefcase. Police found money and drugs in the briefcase and thereafter learned that appellant was released from parole. Appellant was arrested and convicted of drug possession. Appellant challenged his conviction, and the court held that the initial entry was unconstitutional, but the evidence was neither tainted nor inadmissible because the officers had a good faith belief that appellant was on parole. The court affirmed the conviction, arguing that the U.S. Const. amend. IV's exclusion clause did not apply in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that while the police officers' entry into appellant's motel room was unconstitutional, the officers had a good faith belief for their actions, and the evidence was properly admitted at trial because it was in plain view and the officer later developed probable cause.

Bolsa Chica Land Trust v. Superior Court


No. D029461, No. D030270.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


71 Cal. App. 4th 493; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 850; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 332; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2821; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3619



April 16, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Real Parties in Interest. Petitions for writs of mandamus. Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. 703570. Judith D. McConnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trust's petition is granted in part and the superior court is directed to grant the trust's administrative mandamus petition with respect to the eucalyptus grove; in all other respects, the parties' petitions are denied. Trust to recover its costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners and respondents sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County, (California) in an action which sought a writ of mandamus to invalidate the approval by the California Coastal Commission of development plans for a tract of land. The tract contained environmentally sensitive habitat areas, wetlands and a pond, all of which petitioners sought to protect pursuant to the Coastal Act.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners submitted a petition for writ of mandamus to invalidate the approval by the California Coastal Commission of development plans devised by respondents for a tract of land. Upon judicial review of the administrative decision, both respondents and petitioners appealed. Respondents objected to the court's requirement that a pond be preserved and to the prohibition of their development in a wetlands area. Petitioners disputed the court's conclusion that the Coastal Act allowed relocation of an environmentally sensitive habitat. On appeal, the court reviewed the record and delineated the lower court's standard of review, which was to determine whether the commission's findings were supported by substantial evidence. After a lengthy discussion of the operative aspects of the plan itself and the mandate of the Act, the court refuted the determination that the relocation of the habitat was permissible and reversed this portion of its judgment. However, the lower court was correct in concluding that neither development of the wetlands nor the filling of the pond were permitted under the Act. An assessment of attorney's fees against respondents was also upheld.


OUTCOME: The portion of the lower court's judgment that determined that relocation of an environmentally sensitive habitat from a tract of land to make way for commercial development was found violative of the Coastal Act and reversed. However, the lower court was correct in concluding that neither development of wetlands nor the filling of a pond upon the tract were permitted under the Act.

People v. Hernandez


No. E021166.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


71 Cal. App. 4th 417; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 747; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 324; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2747; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3553



April 14, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part 2.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 6, 1999. Review Denied July 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4939.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super. Ct. No. FCH02030. Ingrid A. Uhler, Judge. *


*  Judge of the San Bernardino Municipal Court, West Valley Division, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, § 6 of the California Constitution.

Original Opinion of October 21, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Cal. App. LEXIS 877.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which convicted him of inflicting corporal injury upon a cohabitant and of being under the influence of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of inflicting corporal injury upon a cohabitant and of being under the influence of methamphetamine. After victim reported being hit, the police went to defendant's home. Defendant told police that he had gotten into an argument with the victim and hit her. The police found drugs, and defendant tested positive to drug use. The jury found defendant had two prior strike convictions and was sentenced to prison for two consecutive 25-year-to-life terms. He appealed, claiming evidence was improperly admitted and his trial counsel was incompetent. The court did not agree with defendant that Cal. Evid. Code § 1370 violated the confrontation clause of the constitution. The court found that absent a case where the trial court relied heavily upon the presence of corroborating evidence in making its determination that a statement bore indicia of reliability, the confrontation clause would not be violated. Additionally, defendant waived the objection to the court's admitting statements made by the victim to the police officer. Finally, defendant was incorrect in contending that the statements did not bear sufficient indicia of reliability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of inflicting corporal injury upon a cohabitant and of being under the influence of methamphetamine, finding the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting statements the victim made to the police officer.

 

369 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Shear


No. C029415.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 278; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 707; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 317; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2633; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3443



April 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review denied July 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 5257.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County. Super. Ct. No. CM009488. Gerald Hermansen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County (California) for being a convicted felon in possession of a firearm in violation of Cal. Penal Code §12021(a)(1) contending that the actions of his Arizona conviction would not have been a felony in California, and that the full faith and credit clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1 required California to honor defendant's right to possess a firearm in Arizona.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his California trial conviction for being a felon in possession of a firearm contending that the conduct he was convicted of in Arizona would not be a felony in California, and that the full faith and credit clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1 required that California honor that under Arizona law, the place of his previous felony conviction, that he was eligible to possess a firearm. The court examined Cal. Penal Code § 12021(a)(1), the statute of defendant's conviction, which stated that any person convicted of a felony under the laws of the United States, of the state of California, or any other state, government, or country who owned, or had in his or her possession or under his or her custody or control, any firearm, was guilty of a felony. The court also examined full faith and credit clause precedent which stated that states could not legislate for each other across state lines so as to preclude a state from prescribing the legal consequences for acts within it. Concluding that California could execute its public policy to preclude convicted felons from possessing firearms within its borders, the trial court judgment against defendant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court against the defendant was affirmed because the court concluded that the full faith and credit clause did not preclude California from carrying out its public policy of prohibiting convicted felons within its borders from possessing firearms merely because the defendant could lawfully possess firearms in Arizona in spite of his previous Arizona felony conviction.

 

370 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Hodges


No. C029795.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


70 Cal. App. 4th 1348; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 619; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 304; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2499; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3225



April 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 14, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4744 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 96F07882. Ronald Robie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence for carrying a concealed firearm within a vehicle, a violation of Cal. Pen. Code § 12025(a), on grounds that his initial detention was unlawful, § 12025(a) was unconstitutionally vague and arbitrarily and irrationally criminalized conduct that minimized the risk of harm from carrying weapons in vehicles, there was insufficient evidence of concealment, and he was denied his right to a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for carrying a concealed firearm within a vehicle, a violation of Cal. Pen. Code § 12025(a). Defendant moved to have the conviction and sentence reversed on multiple grounds. The court denied defendant relief. The court determined that under the test of reasonable certainty, § 12025(a) easily passed muster as a constitutional statute because it described the prohibited conduct in readily understandable terms, using precisely quantified standards. Because the vagueness challenge to the ordinance failed, defendant did not show that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to move to suppress the evidence on this ground. The court held that § 12025(a) could not be said to violate substantive due process on its face because it arbitrarily and irrationally criminalized conduct that reduced the risk of harm from transporting guns in vehicles, because the statute requires that cases transporting weapons be locked. Finally, the court determined that defendant waived the contention that he was denied a fair trial, the challenge to one probation condition, and the imposition of a booking fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for a weapons offense upon a finding that the statute under which he was convicted was constitutional under the test of reasonable certainty, defendant could not sustain his allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel, and the statute did not violate substantive due process on its face.

City of Fresno v. Fresno Firefighters, IAFF Local 753


Nos. F025765, F026444.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 82; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 603; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 302; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2446; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3155



April 1, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4948.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Super. Ct. No. 474551-9. James L. Quaschnick and Stephen Joseph Kane, Judges. * 


*  Judge Quaschnick presided over the trial and rendered the judgment in F025765;. Judge Kane made the order denying attorney fees in F026444.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in No. F025765 is affirmed. The order in No. F026444 is affirmed. The City's cross-appeal is dismissed as moot. The City is awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants state, firefighters' union, and police officers' association, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) an action involving efforts of plaintiffs, city and city council, to repeal portions of § 809 of the Fresno City Charter setting levels below which salaries for police officers and firefighters could not be negotiated.


OVERVIEW: Fresno city firefighters' union, and police association appealed decision in an action involving efforts of the Fresno city council and the City of Fresno to repeal portions of § 809 of the Fresno city charter setting levels below which salaries for police and firefighters could not be negotiated. The court gave effect to the words of Fresno City charter § 809 as a statement of the city's fundamental labor policy, and not merely to the practical effect it had in firefighter and police wage negotiations. The court concluded the unions had no stake under the Meyers-Milias-Brown Act, Cal. Gov't. Code § 3500 et seq., which required cities to meet and confer regarding conditions of employment, in determining whether citizens of Fresno directed an opening bargaining position to be assumed by the city's labor negotiators. The minimum salary formula was not a mandatory subject of bargaining. The court concluded that repeal of charter § 809, with postcontract effects only, was not within the scope of the zipper clause and placing a repeal proposal on the ballot did not change the status quo so long as wages continued to be set consistent with the formula during negotiations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed where the city's actions were not subject to the mandatory meet-and-confer requirements of the Meyers-Milias-Brown Act. The city was not required to bargain to impasse prior to taking the unilateral step of placing the issue of repeal before the electorate. The city's cross-appeal was dismissed as moot.

Carmel Valley Fire Protection Dist. v. State of California


B113383


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


70 Cal. App. 4th 1525; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 466; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 296; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2387; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3097



March 31, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 30, 1999 (S078828), Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4230.
Reprinted without Change in the Review Granted Opinions Cumulative Supplement (July 1999) to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in the January 2001 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California Opinion of April 5, 2001, Reported at: 25 Cal. 4th 287.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS041545. Robert E. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying appellants an ordinary and administrative mandate and holding that clothing and equipment requirements imposed by the Executive Orders were validly suspended by Cal. Gov't Code § 17581.


OVERVIEW: Executive Orders were adopted establishing minimum requirements for personal protective clothing and equipment for fire fighters. As a result of these Executive Orders, all state employers, including local governmental agencies, were required to provide the designated clothing and equipment for their fire fighting employees. When the state started to run out of money, respondents enacted a statute that suspended compliance with state-mandated programs when specified conditions were met. A decision that the state was not obligated to reimburse appellants for the funds it spent in compliance with the Executive Orders was reversed and remanded. Cal. Gov't Code § 17581 was nothing more than an impermissible attempt to exercise supervisorial control over the manner in which the executive branch executed the laws enacted by the legislature. The legislature attempted to exercise an unconstitutional veto power over the executive branch's administration of laws. Section 17581 was constitutionally infirm as applied in this case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the denial of a mandate because the separation of powers doctrine precluded the legislature's exercise of supervisorial control or veto power over executive orders as contained in the statute.

People v. Kroncke


No. A077974.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


70 Cal. App. 4th 1535; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 493; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 284; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2373; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3078



March 31, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II.C and II.D.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 4834.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County. Super. Ct. No. 84944A. William H. Stephens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed his conviction entered in the Superior Court of Marin County (California), for failure to stop and report an accident as required by the Cal. Veh. Code §§ 20001, 20003, and for giving false information to a police officer in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 31.


OVERVIEW: Defendant driver picked up a tourist, who suddenly jumped from defendant's car while the car was moving. Defendant was shocked and did not stop immediately. Instead he continued down the road, turned around, and returned to the scene. When questioned about the accident, defendant did not immediately inform the investigating officer of his involvement. Defendant eventually provided the officer with a detailed statement concerning the events leading up to accident. Defendant was subsequently convicted of failing to report an accident in violation of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 20001, 20003. Defendant appealed his conviction and contended that the reporting statutes violated his Fifth Amendment right to be free from self-incrimination. The court discussed the legislative history behind the statute, methods of statutory interpretation, and the Fifth Amendment issue. The court concluded that the purpose of the reporting statutes was to promote satisfaction of civil liabilities arising from automobile accidents. The court also rejected defendant's contention that no reportable accident had occurred; thus, he was not obligated to contact police. Thus, defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court noted that the legitimate aim of California's compulsory reporting statutes were civil remediation and regulation of drivers who use the roadways in California. A driver's right to be free from being compelled to be a witness against himself was not violated by the reporting statutes. Thus, defendant driver's conviction for failure to report an accident was affirmed.

Bergeron v. Department of Health Services


No. F029448.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


71 Cal. App. 4th 17; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 481; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 300; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3115; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2407



March 31, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Super. Ct. No. 97-179181. Patrick J. O'Hara, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California) denying appellant's petition for writ of mandate requiring respondents to hold an administrative hearing as to respondents' right to withhold payment of fees claimed by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a dentist whose patients were indigents who were beneficiaries of Medi-Cal services. Appellant submitted the bills to respondent, and respondent reviewed the bills in accordance with the regulatory scheme before making payment. A search warrant for appellant's business offices was obtained as a result of an ongoing fraud investigation concerning appellant's billing practices. Respondents provided appellant with notification that payments were to be withheld. A criminal complaint was filed charging appellant with fraud for billing for services not provided. Denial of appellant's petition for a writ of mandate was affirmed. There was no duty to conduct a hearing under statute or regulation. Respondents were permitted pursuant to 42 C.F.R. § 455.23 (1998) to withhold payments to appellant when provided with reliable evidence that there was fraud. The search warrant was sufficient under the notice requirements of the regulation. Appellant was told she could submit written evidence for consideration by respondents. The interest in maintaining the integrity of the Medi-Cal system justified the temporary withholding of payments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the writ because due process did not require respondents to hold an administrative hearing as to its right to withhold payment of fees. Given the procedural notice mechanisms and the opportunity afforded appellant to respond to the withholding notice, the dictates of due process were met.

Conservatorship of Angela D.


No. E022410.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


70 Cal. App. 4th 1410; 83 Cal. Rptr. 2d 411; 1999 Cal. App. LEXIS 262; 99 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2337; 99 Daily Journal DAR 3045



March 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Super.Ct.No. RC00121. Joseph E. Johnston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order appealed from is affirmed. Parties to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Conservatee appealed from a probate court order approving the petition filed by respondents, conservatee's parents and coconservators, for an order authorizing the coconservators to give medical consent for conservatee's sterilization under Cal. Prob. Code § 1950 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Conservatee, severely mentally retarded and autistic woman, challenged an order approving petition filed by coconservators for an order authorizing consent for conservatee's sterilization pursuant to Cal. Prob. Code § 1950 et seq. Conservatee contended she was not likely to engage in sexual activity or that supervision was an alternative to sterilization. Conservatee alleged that requirements under Cal. Prob. Code § 1958 were not established and the failure to satisfy all elements was fatal to order. The court concluded § 1958(c) authorized sterilization of incapacitated persons under certain conditions and Cal. Prob. Code § 1959 could not constitutionally be applied to deny coconservators the authorization to consent to sterilization. Section 1959 denied consideration of fact that disabled person may be vulnerable to unlawful sexual conduct by others. The court determined that § 1959 denied to conservatee the reproductive choices available to individuals without disabilities. The provision in § 1959 that made it logically impossible for conservator to make the necessary showing under the chapter was inconsistent with intent of permitting sterilization with appropriate safeguards.


OUTCOME: The order authorizing consent for conservatee's sterilization was affirmed where conservators established beyond a reasonable doubt the requirements of § 1958; the facts were compelling and the proceedings were carried out with diligence and attention to conservatee's best interests.
